However, he also cautions that errors are frequently found on Internet sites and that academics and experts must be vigilant in correcting them.[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-tnr_experts_vigilant_in_correcting_WP_1-221)[Amy Bruckman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amy_Bruckman "Amy Bruckman") has argued that, due to the number of reviewers, "the content of a popular Wikipedia page is actually the most reliable form of information ever created".[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-PC_2021-222) In September 2022, _[The Sydney Morning Herald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Sydney\_Morning\_Herald "The Sydney Morning Herald")_ journalist Liam Mannix noted that: "There's no reason to expect Wikipedia to be accurate... And yet it [is]." Mannix further discussed the multiple studies that have proved Wikipedia to be generally as reliable as _Encyclopædia Britannica_, summarizing that "...turning our back on such an extraordinary resource is... well, a little petty."[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-223)

Critics argue that Wikipedia's open nature and a lack of proper sources for most of the information makes it unreliable.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-TNY_reliability_issues_1-224) Some commentators suggest that Wikipedia may be reliable, but that the reliability of any given article is not clear.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-AcademiaAndWikipedia-225) Editors of traditional [reference works](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reference_work "Reference work") such as the _Encyclopædia Britannica_ have questioned the project's [utility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utility "Utility") and status as an encyclopedia.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-McHenry_2004-226) Wikipedia co-founder [Jimmy Wales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Wales "Jimmy Wales") has claimed that Wikipedia has largely avoided the problem of "fake news" because the Wikipedia community regularly debates the quality of sources in articles.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-227)

| External videos |
| --- |
| ![Image 17: video icon](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/20px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png)[Inside Wikipedia– Attack of the PR Industry](https://www.dw.de/inside-wikipedia-attack-of-the-pr-industry/av-17745881), [Deutsche Welle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsche_Welle "Deutsche Welle"), 7:13 mins[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-dw-228) |

Wikipedia's open structure inherently makes it an easy target for [Internet trolls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_troll "Internet troll"), [spammers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spamming "Spamming"), and various forms of paid advocacy seen as counterproductive to the maintenance of a neutral and verifiable online encyclopedia.[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Torsten_Kleinz-104)[[W 50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-citizendium_WP_trolling_issues_1-229) In response to [paid advocacy editing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conflict-of-interest_editing_on_Wikipedia "Conflict-of-interest editing on Wikipedia") and undisclosed editing issues, Wikipedia was reported in an article in _The Wall Street Journal_ to have strengthened its rules and laws against undisclosed editing.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-ReferenceA-230) The article stated that: "Beginning Monday [from the date of the article, June 16, 2014], changes in Wikipedia's terms of use will require anyone paid to edit articles to disclose that arrangement. [Katherine Maher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katherine_Maher "Katherine Maher"), the nonprofit Wikimedia Foundation's chief communications officer, said the changes address a sentiment among volunteer editors that 'we're not an advertising service; we're an encyclopedia.'"[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-ReferenceA-230)[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-DeathByWikipedia-231)[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-cnet_politicians_and_WP_1-232)[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-msnbc_MS_cash_for_WP_edits_1-233)[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Seeing_Corporate_Fingerprints-234) These issues, among others, had been parodied since the first decade of Wikipedia, notably by [Stephen Colbert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Colbert "Stephen Colbert") on _[The Colbert Report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Colbert\_Report "The Colbert Report")_.[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-wikiality-235)

### Discouragement in education

Some university lecturers discourage students from citing any encyclopedia in [academic work](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academia "Academia"), preferring [primary sources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_source "Primary source");[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WideWorldOfWikipedia-236) some specifically prohibit Wikipedia citations.[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-insidehighered_against_WP_1-237)[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-insidehighered_wiki_no_cite-238) Wales stresses that encyclopedias of any type are not usually appropriate to use as citable sources, and should not be relied upon as authoritative.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-AWorkInProgress-239) Wales once (2006 or earlier) said he receives about ten emails weekly from students saying they got failing grades on papers because they cited Wikipedia; he told the students they got what they deserved. "For God's sake, you're in college; don't cite the encyclopedia", he said.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-240)

In February 2007, an article in _[The Harvard Crimson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Harvard\_Crimson "The Harvard Crimson")_ newspaper reported that a few of the professors at [Harvard University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harvard_University "Harvard University") were including Wikipedia articles in their [syllabi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syllabus "Syllabus"), although without realizing the articles might change.[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-thecrimson_wiki_debate-241) In June 2007, [Michael Gorman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Gorman_(librarian) "Michael Gorman (librarian)"), former president of the [American Library Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Library_Association "American Library Association"), condemned Wikipedia, along with Google, stating that academics who endorse the use of Wikipedia are "the intellectual equivalent of a dietitian who recommends a steady diet of Big Macs with everything".[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-stothart-242)

A 2020 research study published in _[Studies in Higher Education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Studies\_in\_Higher\_Education "Studies in Higher Education")_ argued that Wikipedia could be applied in the higher education "[flipped classroom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flipped_classroom "Flipped classroom")", an educational model where students learn before coming to class and apply it in classroom activities. The experimental group was instructed to learn before class and get immediate feedback before going in (the flipped classroom model), while the control group was given direct instructions in class (the conventional classroom model). The groups were then instructed to collaboratively develop Wikipedia entries, which would be graded in quality after the study. The results showed that the experimental group yielded more Wikipedia entries and received higher grades in quality. The study concluded that learning with Wikipedia in flipped classrooms was more effective than in conventional classrooms, demonstrating Wikipedia could be used as an educational tool in higher education.[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-243)

#### Medical information

On March 5, 2014, Julie Beck writing for _[The Atlantic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Atlantic "The Atlantic")_ magazine in an article titled "Doctors' #1 Source for Healthcare Information: Wikipedia", stated that "Fifty percent of physicians look up conditions on the (Wikipedia) site, and some are editing articles themselves to improve the quality of available information."[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:10-244) Beck continued to detail in this article new programs of [Amin Azzam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amin_Azzam "Amin Azzam") at the [University of San Francisco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_San_Francisco "University of San Francisco") to offer medical school courses to medical students for learning to edit and improve [Wikipedia articles on health-related issues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_information_on_Wikipedia "Health information on Wikipedia"), as well as internal quality control programs within Wikipedia organized by [James Heilman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Heilman "James Heilman") to improve a group of 200 health-related articles of central medical importance up to Wikipedia's highest standard of articles using its Featured Article and Good Article peer-review evaluation process.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:10-244) In a May 7, 2014, follow-up article in _The Atlantic_ titled "Can Wikipedia Ever Be a Definitive Medical Text?", Julie Beck quotes WikiProject Medicine's James Heilman as stating: "Just because a reference is peer-reviewed doesn't mean it's a high-quality reference."[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-theatlantic.com-245) Beck added that: "Wikipedia has its own peer review process before articles can be classified as 'good' or 'featured'. Heilman, who has participated in that process before, says 'less than one percent' of Wikipedia's medical articles have passed."[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-theatlantic.com-245)

### Coverage of topics and systemic bias

Wikipedia seeks to create a summary of all human knowledge in the form of an online encyclopedia, with each topic covered encyclopedically in one article. Since it has [terabytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byte#Multiple-byte_units "Byte") of [disk space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disk_space "Disk space"), it can have far more topics than can be covered by any printed encyclopedia.[[W 51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-246) The exact degree and manner of coverage on Wikipedia is under constant review by its editors, and disagreements are not uncommon (see [deletionism and inclusionism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deletionism_and_inclusionism_in_Wikipedia "Deletionism and inclusionism in Wikipedia")).[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Economist_disagreements_not_uncommon-247)[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-telegraph_WP_torn_apart_1-248) Wikipedia contains materials that some people may find objectionable, offensive, or pornographic.[[W 52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-249) The "Wikipedia is not censored" policy has sometimes proved controversial: in 2008, Wikipedia rejected an online petition against the inclusion of [images of Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Online_petition_on_Wikipedia_Muhammad_article "Online petition on Wikipedia Muhammad article") in the [English edition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Wikipedia "English Wikipedia") of its [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad "Muhammad") article, citing this policy.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-250) The presence of politically, religiously, and pornographically sensitive materials in Wikipedia has led to the [censorship of Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Censorship_of_Wikipedia "Censorship of Wikipedia") by national authorities in China[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Taylor-251) and Pakistan,[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-washington_post_state_censorship_1-252) among other countries.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-253)[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-254)[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-255)

Through its "Wikipedia Loves Libraries" program, Wikipedia has partnered with major public libraries such as the [New York Public Library for the Performing Arts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Public_Library_for_the_Performing_Arts "New York Public Library for the Performing Arts") to expand its coverage of underrepresented subjects and articles.[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-NYT_subjects_and_articles-256) A 2011 study conducted by researchers at the [University of Minnesota](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Minnesota "University of Minnesota") indicated that male and female editors focus on different coverage topics. There was a greater concentration of females in the "people and arts" category, while males focus more on "geography and science".[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-257) An editorial in _[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Guardian "The Guardian")_ in 2014 claimed that more effort went into providing references for [a list of female porn actors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_pornographic_performers_by_decade "List of pornographic performers by decade") than a [list of women writers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_women_writers "List of women writers").[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-GuardianAugust2014-258)

#### Systemic biases

Wikipedia's policies may limit "its capacity for truly representing global knowledge". For example, Wikipedia only considers published sources to be reliable. [Oral knowledge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oral_knowledge "Oral knowledge") of Indigenous cultures is not always reflected in print. Marginalized topics are also more likely to lack significant coverage in reliable sources. Wikipedia's content is therefore limited as a result of larger systemic biases.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDowellVetter202237,_38,_47-259)

[Academic studies of Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academic_studies_about_Wikipedia "Academic studies about Wikipedia") have shown that the average contributor to the English Wikipedia is an educated, technically inclined white male, aged 15–49, from a developed, predominantly Christian country.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Livingstone2010-260) The corresponding point of view (POV) is over-represented.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Hube2017-261)[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:132-208) This systemic bias in editor demographic results in [cultural bias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_bias "Cultural bias"), [gender bias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_bias_on_Wikipedia "Gender bias on Wikipedia"), and [geographical bias on Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geographical_bias_on_Wikipedia "Geographical bias on Wikipedia").[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:32-262)[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-263) There are two broad types of bias, which are _implicit_ (when a topic is omitted) and _explicit_ (when a certain POV is over-represented in an article or by references).[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Hube2017-261)

Interdisciplinary scholarly assessments of Wikipedia articles have found that while articles are typically accurate and free of misinformation, they are also typically incomplete and fail to present all perspectives with a [neutral point of view](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neutrality_(philosophy) "Neutrality (philosophy)").[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:32-262) In 2011, Wales claimed that the unevenness of coverage is a reflection of the demography of the editors, citing for example "biographies of famous women through history and issues surrounding early childcare".[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-wiki-women-49) The October 22, 2013, essay by Tom Simonite in MIT's _Technology Review_ titled "The Decline of Wikipedia" discussed the effect of systemic bias and [policy creep](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criticism_of_Wikipedia#Excessive_regulation "Criticism of Wikipedia") on the [downward trend in the number of editors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#English_Wikipedia_editor_numbers).[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Simonite-2013-50)

Research conducted by Mark Graham of the [Oxford Internet Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_Internet_Institute "Oxford Internet Institute") in 2009 indicated that the geographic distribution of article topics is highly uneven, with Africa being the most underrepresented.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-264) Across 30 language editions of Wikipedia, historical articles and sections are generally [Eurocentric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurocentric "Eurocentric") and focused on recent events.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-265)

### Explicit content

Wikipedia has been criticized for allowing information about graphic content.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-266) Articles depicting what some critics have called objectionable content (such as [feces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feces "Feces"), [cadaver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cadaver "Cadaver"), [human penis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_penis "Human penis"), [vulva](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulva "Vulva"), and nudity) contain graphic pictures and detailed information easily available to anyone with access to the internet, including children.[[W 53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-267) The site also includes [sexual content](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_content "Sexual content") such as images and videos of [masturbation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masturbation "Masturbation") and [ejaculation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ejaculation "Ejaculation"), illustrations of [zoophilia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoophilia "Zoophilia"), and photos from [hardcore pornographic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hardcore_pornography "Hardcore pornography") films in its articles. It also has non-sexual [photographs of nude children](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_nudity "Child nudity").[[W 54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-268)

The Wikipedia article about _[Virgin Killer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgin\_Killer "Virgin Killer")_—a 1976 album from the German rock band [Scorpions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scorpions_(band) "Scorpions (band)")—features a picture of the album's original cover, which depicts a naked [prepubescent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preadolescence#Prepubescence,_puberty,_and_age_range "Preadolescence") girl. The original release cover caused controversy and was replaced in some countries. In December 2008, access to the Wikipedia article _Virgin Killer_ was blocked for four days by most [Internet service providers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_service_provider "Internet service provider") in the United Kingdom after the [Internet Watch Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_Watch_Foundation "Internet Watch Foundation") (IWF) decided the album cover was a potentially illegal indecent image and added the article's URL to a "blacklist" it supplies to British internet service providers.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Register_ISP_censorship-269)

In April 2010, Sanger wrote a letter to the Federal Bureau of Investigation, outlining his concerns that two categories of images on [Wikimedia Commons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Commons "Wikimedia Commons") contained child pornography, and were in violation of [US federal obscenity law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_obscenity_law "United States obscenity law").[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-270)[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Inquirer_child_abuse_allegations-271) Sanger later clarified that the images, which were related to [pedophilia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pedophilia "Pedophilia") and one about [lolicon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lolicon "Lolicon"), were not of real children, but said that they constituted "obscene visual representations of the sexual abuse of children", under the [PROTECT Act of 2003](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_pornography_laws_in_the_United_States#1466A_%E2%80%93_Obscene_visual_representations_of_the_sexual_abuse_of_children "Child pornography laws in the United States").[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-The_Register-April-272) That law bans photographic child pornography and cartoon images and drawings of children that are [obscene under American law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obscenity#United_States_obscenity_law "Obscenity").[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-The_Register-April-272) Sanger also expressed concerns about access to the images on Wikipedia in schools.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-TET_child_porn_accusations-273)

[Wikimedia Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Foundation "Wikimedia Foundation") spokesman Jay Walsh strongly rejected Sanger's accusation,[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-AFP-274) saying that Wikipedia did not have "material we would deem to be illegal. If we did, we would remove it."[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-AFP-274) Following the complaint by Sanger, Wales deleted sexual images without consulting the community. After some editors who volunteered to maintain the site argued that the decision to delete had been made hastily, Wales voluntarily gave up some of the powers he had held up to that time as part of his co-founder status. He wrote in a message to the Wikimedia Foundation mailing-list that this action was "in the interest of encouraging this discussion to be about real philosophical/content issues, rather than be about me and how quickly I acted".[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-BBC_News_Wales_cedes_rights-275) Critics, including [Wikipediocracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipediocracy "Wikipediocracy"), noticed that many of the pornographic images deleted from Wikipedia since 2010 have reappeared.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-XBIZ-276)

### Privacy

One [privacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privacy "Privacy") concern in the case of Wikipedia regards one's right to remain a [private citizen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_citizen "Private citizen") rather than a [public figure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_figure "Public figure") in the eyes of the law.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-277)[[g]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-278) It is a battle between the right to be anonymous in [cyberspace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyberspace "Cyberspace") and the right to be anonymous in [real life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_life "Real life"). The Wikimedia Foundation's [privacy policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privacy_policy "Privacy policy") states, "we believe that you shouldn't have to provide personal information to participate in the free knowledge movement", and states that "personal information" may be shared "For legal reasons", "To Protect You, Ourselves & Others", or "To Understand & Experiment".[[W 55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-279)

In January 2006, a German court ordered the [German Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Wikipedia "German Wikipedia") shut down within Germany because it stated the full name of [Boris Floricic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tron_(hacker) "Tron (hacker)"), aka "Tron", a deceased hacker. On February 9, 2006, the injunction against Wikimedia Deutschland was overturned, with the court rejecting the notion that Tron's [right to privacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_to_privacy "Right to privacy") or that of his parents was being violated.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-heise_Tron_public_issue_1-280)

Wikipedia has a "Volunteer Response Team" that uses Znuny, a [free and open-source software](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software "Free and open-source software") fork of [OTRS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OTRS "OTRS")[[W 56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-281) to handle queries without having to reveal the identities of the involved parties. This is used, for example, in confirming the permission for using individual images and other media in the project.[[W 57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-282)

In late April 2023, Wikimedia Foundation announced that Wikipedia will not submit to any age verifications that may be required by the UK's [Online Safety Bill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Online_Safety_Act_2023 "Online Safety Act 2023") legislation. Rebecca MacKinnon of the Wikimedia Foundation said that such checks would run counter to the website's commitment to minimal data collection on its contributors and readers.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-283)

### Sexism

Wikipedia was described in 2015 as harboring a battleground culture of [sexism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexism "Sexism") and [harassment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harassment "Harassment").[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Paling-284)[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-285) The perceived tolerance of abusive language was a reason put forth in 2013 for the gender gap in Wikipedia editorship.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-286)[Edit-a-thons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edit-a-thon "Edit-a-thon") have been held to encourage female editors and increase the coverage of women's topics.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-287)

In May 2018, a Wikipedia editor rejected a submitted article about [Donna Strickland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donna_Strickland "Donna Strickland") due to lack of coverage in the media.[[W 58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-288)[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:11-289) Five months later, Strickland won a [Nobel Prize in Physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics "Nobel Prize in Physics") "for groundbreaking inventions in the field of laser physics", becoming the third woman to ever receive the award.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:11-289)[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-290) Prior to winning the award, Strickland's only mention on Wikipedia was in the article about her collaborator and co-winner of the award [Gérard Mourou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%A9rard_Mourou "Gérard Mourou").[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:11-289) Her exclusion from Wikipedia led to accusations of sexism, but Corinne Purtill writing for _[Quartz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quartz\_(publication) "Quartz (publication)")_ argued that "it's also a pointed lesson in the hazards of gender bias in media, and of the broader consequences of underrepresentation."[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:12-291) Purtill attributes the issue to the gender bias in media coverage.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:12-291)

A comprehensive 2008 survey, published in 2016, by Julia B. Bear of [Stony Brook University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stony_Brook_University "Stony Brook University")'s College of Business and Benjamin Collier of [Carnegie Mellon University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University "Carnegie Mellon University") found significant gender differences in confidence in expertise, discomfort with editing, and response to critical feedback. "Women reported less confidence in their expertise, expressed greater discomfort with editing (which typically involves conflict), and reported more negative responses to critical feedback compared to men."[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-292)

Operation
---------

### Wikimedia Foundation and affiliate movements

[![Image 18: Katherine Maher in 2016. She is seen with light skin, blonde hair, and blue eyes. She is seen wearing a black shirt.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Katherine_Maher.jpg/250px-Katherine_Maher.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Katherine_Maher.jpg)

[Katherine Maher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katherine_Maher "Katherine Maher"), the third executive director of Wikimedia, served from 2016 to 2021.

Wikipedia is hosted and funded by the [Wikimedia Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Foundation "Wikimedia Foundation"), a non-profit organization which also operates Wikipedia-related projects such as [Wiktionary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiktionary "Wiktionary") and [Wikibooks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikibooks "Wikibooks").[[W 59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-293) The foundation relies on public contributions and grants to fund its mission.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-294)[[W 60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-financialstatements-295) The foundation's 2020 Internal Revenue Service [Form 990](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Form_990 "Form 990") shows revenue of $124.6 million and expenses of almost $112.2 million, with assets of about $191.2 million and liabilities of almost $11 million.[[W 61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-296)

In May 2014, Wikimedia Foundation named [Lila Tretikov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lila_Tretikov "Lila Tretikov") as its second executive director, taking over for Sue Gardner.[[W 62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-297)_The_ _Wall Street Journal_ reported on May 1, 2014, that Tretikov's information technology background, from her years at University of California offers Wikipedia an opportunity to develop in more concentrated directions guided by her often repeated position statement that, "Information, like air, wants to be free."[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Jeff_Elder_2014-298)[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-nytimes.com-299) The same _Wall Street Journal_ article reported these directions of development according to an interview with spokesman Jay Walsh of Wikimedia, who "said Tretikov would address that issue ([paid advocacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conflict-of-interest_editing_on_Wikipedia "Conflict-of-interest editing on Wikipedia")) as a priority. 'We are really pushing toward more transparency... We are reinforcing that paid advocacy is not welcome.' Initiatives to involve greater diversity of contributors, better mobile support of Wikipedia, new geo-location tools to find local content more easily, and more tools for users in the second and third world are also priorities", Walsh said.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Jeff_Elder_2014-298)

Following the departure of Tretikov from Wikipedia due to issues concerning the use of the "superprotection" feature which some language versions of Wikipedia have adopted,[[W 63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-300)[Katherine Maher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katherine_Maher "Katherine Maher") became the third executive director of the Wikimedia Foundation in June 2016.[[W 64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-301) Maher stated that one of her priorities would be the issue of editor harassment endemic to Wikipedia as identified by the Wikipedia board in December. She said to _[Bloomberg Businessweek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloomberg\_Businessweek "Bloomberg Businessweek")_ regarding the harassment issue that: "It establishes a sense within the community that this is a priority... [and that correction requires that] it has to be more than words."[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Bloomberg_2016-175)

Maher served as executive director until April 2021.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-axios-302)[Maryana Iskander](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maryana_Iskander "Maryana Iskander") was named the incoming CEO in September 2021, and took over that role in January 2022. She stated that one of her focuses would be increasing diversity in the Wikimedia community.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-303)

Wikipedia is also supported by many organizations and groups that are affiliated with the Wikimedia Foundation but independently-run, called [Wikimedia movement affiliates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_movement_affiliates "Wikimedia movement affiliates"). These include [Wikimedia chapters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Wikimedia_chapters "List of Wikimedia chapters") (which are national or sub-national organizations, such as Wikimedia Deutschland and Wikimedia France), thematic organizations (such as Amical Wikimedia for the [Catalan language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalan_language "Catalan language") community), and user groups. These affiliates participate in the promotion, development, and funding of Wikipedia.[[W 65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-304)

### Software operations and support

The operation of Wikipedia depends on [MediaWiki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MediaWiki "MediaWiki"), a custom-made, [free](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_software "Free software") and open source [wiki software](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiki_software "Wiki software") platform written in [PHP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PHP "PHP") and built upon the [MySQL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MySQL "MySQL") database system.[[W 66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-nedworks_database_system-305) The software incorporates programming features such as a [macro language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macro_(computer_science) "Macro (computer science)"), [variables](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_(programming) "Variable (programming)"), a [transclusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transclusion "Transclusion") system for [templates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_template_system "Web template system"), and [URL redirection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/URL_redirection "URL redirection").[[W 67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-306) MediaWiki is licensed under the [GNU General Public License](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License "GNU General Public License") (GPL) and it is used by all Wikimedia projects, as well as many other wiki projects.[[W 66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-nedworks_database_system-305)[[W 68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-307) Originally, Wikipedia ran on [UseModWiki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UseModWiki "UseModWiki") written in [Perl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perl "Perl") by Clifford Adams (Phase I), which initially required [CamelCase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CamelCase "CamelCase") for article hyperlinks; the present double bracket style was incorporated later.[[W 69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-308) Starting in January 2002 (Phase II), Wikipedia began running on a [PHP wiki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PhpWiki "PhpWiki") engine with a MySQL database; this software was custom-made for Wikipedia by [Magnus Manske](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnus_Manske "Magnus Manske"). The Phase II software was repeatedly modified to accommodate the [exponentially increasing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exponential_growth "Exponential growth") demand. In July 2002 (Phase III), Wikipedia shifted to the third-generation software, MediaWiki, originally written by [Lee Daniel Crocker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lee_Daniel_Crocker "Lee Daniel Crocker").

Several MediaWiki extensions are installed to extend the functionality of the MediaWiki software.[[W 70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WP_extensions_installed-309) In April 2005, a [Lucene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucene "Lucene") extension[[W 71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-310)[[W 72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-311) was added to MediaWiki's built-in search and Wikipedia switched from MySQL to Lucene for searching. Lucene was later replaced by CirrusSearch which is based on [Elasticsearch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elasticsearch "Elasticsearch").[[W 73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-312) In July 2013, after extensive beta testing, a [WYSIWYG](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WYSIWYG "WYSIWYG") (What You See Is What You Get) extension, [VisualEditor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VisualEditor "VisualEditor"), was opened to public use.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-thenextwebve-313)[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-314)[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-TheEconomistVE-315) It was met with much rejection and criticism, and was described as "slow and buggy".[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Orlowski,_Andrew-316) The feature was changed from opt-out to opt-in afterward.[[W 74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-317)

### Automated editing

Computer programs called [bots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_bot "Internet bot") have often been used to perform simple and repetitive tasks, such as correcting common misspellings and stylistic issues, or to start articles such as geography entries in a standard format from statistical data.[[W 75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-318)[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-meetbots-319)[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-320) One controversial contributor, [Sverker Johansson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sverker_Johansson "Sverker Johansson"), created articles with his bot [Lsjbot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lsjbot "Lsjbot"), which was reported to create up to 10,000 articles on the Swedish Wikipedia on certain days.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-321) Additionally, there are bots designed to automatically notify editors when they make common editing errors (such as unmatched quotes or unmatched parentheses).[[W 76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-322) Edits falsely identified by bots as the work of a banned editor can be restored by other editors. An anti-vandal bot is programmed to detect and revert vandalism quickly.[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-meetbots-319) Bots are able to indicate edits from particular accounts or [IP address](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IP_address "IP address") ranges, as occurred at the time of the shooting down of the [MH17 jet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaysia_Airlines_Flight_17 "Malaysia Airlines Flight 17") in July 2014 when it was reported that edits were made via IPs controlled by the Russian government.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-323) Bots on Wikipedia must be approved before activation.[[W 77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-324) According to [Andrew Lih](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Lih "Andrew Lih"), the current expansion of Wikipedia to millions of articles would be difficult to envision without the use of such bots.[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-325)

### Hardware operations and support

[![Image 19: Diagram showing flow of data between Wikipedia's servers.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Wikipedia_webrequest_2022.png/250px-Wikipedia_webrequest_2022.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wikipedia_webrequest_2022.png)

Overview of system architecture as of August 2022

As of 2021, page requests are first passed to a front-end layer of [Varnish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Varnish_(software) "Varnish (software)") caching servers and back-end layer [caching](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caching "Caching") is done by [Apache Traffic Server](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apache_Traffic_Server "Apache Traffic Server").[[W 78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:14-326) Requests that cannot be served from the Varnish cache are sent to load-balancing servers running the [Linux Virtual Server](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linux_Virtual_Server "Linux Virtual Server") software, which in turn pass them to one of the Apache web servers for page rendering from the database.[[W 78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:14-326) The web servers deliver pages as requested, performing page rendering for all the language editions of Wikipedia. To increase speed further, rendered pages are cached in a distributed memory cache until invalidated, allowing page rendering to be skipped entirely for most common page accesses.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-327)

Wikipedia currently runs on dedicated [clusters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_cluster "Computer cluster") of [Linux](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linux "Linux") servers running the [Debian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Debian "Debian") operating system.[[W 79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-328) By January 22, 2013, Wikipedia had migrated its primary data center to an [Equinix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equinix "Equinix") facility in [Ashburn, Virginia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashburn,_Virginia "Ashburn, Virginia").[[W 80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:0-329)[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-330) In 2017, Wikipedia installed a caching cluster in an Equinix facility in [Singapore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Singapore "Singapore"), the first of its kind in Asia.[[W 81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-331) In 2022, a caching data center was opened in [Marseille](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marseille "Marseille"), France.[[W 82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-332) In 2024, a caching data center was opened in [São Paulo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo "São Paulo"), the first of its kind in South America.[[W 83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Magru-333) As of November 2024, caching clusters are located in [Amsterdam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amsterdam "Amsterdam"), San Francisco, Singapore, Marseille, and São Paulo.[[W 84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:13-334)[[W 85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-335)

### Internal research and operational development

Following growing amounts of incoming donations in 2013 exceeding seven digits,[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Simonite-2013-50) the Foundation has reached a threshold of assets which qualify its consideration under the principles of [industrial organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_organization "Industrial organization") economics to indicate the need for the re-investment of donations into the internal research and development of the Foundation.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-autogenerated5-336) Two projects of such internal research and development have been the creation of a Visual Editor and the "Thank" tab in the edit history, which were developed to improve issues of editor attrition.[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Simonite-2013-50)[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Orlowski,_Andrew-316) The estimates for reinvestment by industrial organizations into internal research and development was studied by [Adam Jaffe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam_B._Jaffe "Adam B. Jaffe"), who recorded that the range of 4% to 25% annually was to be recommended, with high-end technology requiring the higher level of support for internal reinvestment.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:15-337) At the 2013 level of contributions for Wikimedia presently documented as 45 million dollars,[[W 86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-338) the computed budget level recommended by Jaffe for reinvestment into internal research and development is between 1.8 million and 11.3 million dollars annually.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:15-337) In 2019, the level of contributions were reported by the Wikimedia Foundation as being at $120 million annually,[[W 87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-339) updating the Jaffe estimates for the higher level of support to between $3.08 million and $19.2 million annually.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:15-337)

### Internal news publications

Multiple Wikimedia projects have internal news publications. [Wikimedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Foundation "Wikimedia Foundation")'s online newspaper _[The Signpost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Signpost "The Signpost")_ was founded in 2005 by Michael Snow, a Wikipedia administrator who would join the Wikimedia Foundation's board of trustees in 2008.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-340)[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-341) The publication covers news and events from the English Wikipedia, the Wikimedia Foundation, and [Wikipedia's sister projects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Foundation#Projects_and_initiatives "Wikimedia Foundation").[[W 88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-342)

### The Wikipedia Library

[![Image 20](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Wikipedia_Library_owl.svg/190px-Wikipedia_Library_owl.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wikipedia_Library_owl.svg)

Wikipedia Library

Wikipedia editors sometimes struggle to access paywalled sources needed to improve a subject.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDowellVetter202264-343) The Wikipedia Library is a resource for Wikipedia editors which provides free access to a wide range of [digital publications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_publishing "Electronic publishing"), so that they can consult and cite these while editing the encyclopedia.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-orlowitz-344)[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-bna-345) Over 60 publishers have partnered with The Wikipedia Library to provide access to their resources: when [ICE Publishing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ICE_Publishing "ICE Publishing") joined in 2020, a spokesman said "By enabling free access to our content for Wikipedia editors, we hope to further the research community's resources – creating and updating Wikipedia entries on civil engineering which are read by thousands of monthly readers."[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-hall-346)

Access to content
-----------------

### Content licensing

When the project was started in 2001, all text in Wikipedia was covered by the [GNU Free Documentation License](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GNU_Free_Documentation_License "GNU Free Documentation License") (GFDL), a [copyleft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copyleft "Copyleft") license permitting the redistribution, creation of derivative works, and commercial use of content while authors retain copyright of their work.[[W 89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Wikipedia:Copyrights-347) The GFDL was created for software manuals that come with [free software](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_software "Free software") programs licensed under the [GPL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License "GNU General Public License"). This made it a poor choice for a general reference work: for example, the GFDL requires the reprints of materials from Wikipedia to come with a full copy of the GFDL text.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-348) In December 2002, the [Creative Commons license](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creative_Commons_license "Creative Commons license") was released; it was specifically designed for creative works in general, not just for software manuals. The Wikipedia project sought the switch to the Creative Commons.[[W 90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WPF_switch_to_CC-349) Because the GFDL and Creative Commons were incompatible, in November 2008, following the request of the project, the [Free Software Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation "Free Software Foundation") (FSF) released a new version of the GFDL designed specifically to allow Wikipedia to relicense its content to CC BY-SA by August 1, 2009.[[W 91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-350) In April 2009, Wikipedia and its sister projects held a community-wide referendum which decided the switch in June 2009.[[W 92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-voteresult-351)[[W 93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-MW_licensing_QA-352)[[W 94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-MW_licensing_timeline_1-353)[[W 95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WP_blog_license_migration-354)

The handling of media files (e.g. image files) varies across language editions. Some language editions, such as the English Wikipedia, include non-free image files under [fair use](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_use "Fair use") doctrine,[[W 96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-355) while the others have opted not to, in part because of the lack of fair use doctrines in their home countries (e.g. in [Japanese copyright law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copyright_law_of_Japan "Copyright law of Japan")). Media files covered by [free content](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_content "Free content") licenses (e.g. [Creative Commons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creative_Commons "Creative Commons")' [CC BY-SA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CC_BY-SA "CC BY-SA")) are shared across language editions via [Wikimedia Commons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Commons "Wikimedia Commons") repository, a project operated by the Wikimedia Foundation.[[W 97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-356) Wikipedia's accommodation of varying international copyright laws regarding images has led some to observe that its photographic coverage of topics lags behind the quality of the encyclopedic text.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-NYT_photos_on_WP-357) The Wikimedia Foundation is not a licensor of content on Wikipedia or its related projects but merely a hosting service for contributors to and licensors of Wikipedia, a position which was successfully defended in 2004 in a court in France.[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-reuters_French_defamation_case-358)[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-ars_tech_WP_dumb_suing_case-359)

### Methods of access

Because Wikipedia content is distributed under an open license, anyone can reuse or re-distribute it at no charge.[[W 98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-360) The content of Wikipedia has been published in many forms, both online and offline, outside the Wikipedia website.

Thousands of "[mirror sites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirror_site "Mirror site")" exist that republish content from Wikipedia; two prominent ones that also include content from other reference sources are [Reference.com](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reference.com "Reference.com") and [Answers.com](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Answers.com "Answers.com").[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-361)[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-362) Another example is [Wapedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wapedia "Wapedia"), which began to display Wikipedia content in a mobile-device-friendly format before Wikipedia itself did.[[W 99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:16-363) Some web [search engines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Search_engine "Search engine") make special use of Wikipedia content when displaying search results: examples include [Microsoft Bing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Bing "Microsoft Bing") (via technology gained from [Powerset](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Powerset_(company) "Powerset (company)"))[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-bing_WP_research_and_referencing-364) and [DuckDuckGo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DuckDuckGo "DuckDuckGo").

Collections of Wikipedia articles have been published on [optical discs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_disc "Optical disc"). An English version released in 2006 contained about 2,000 articles.[[W 100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-365) The Polish-language version from 2006 contains nearly 240,000 articles,[[W 101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WM_polish_WP_on_dvd-366) the German-language version from 2007/2008 contains over 620,000 articles,[[W 102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-367) and the Spanish-language version from 2011 contains 886,000 articles.[[W 103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-368) Additionally, "Wikipedia for Schools", the Wikipedia series of CDs / DVDs produced by Wikipedia and [SOS Children](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SOS_Children%27s_Villages_UK "SOS Children's Villages UK"), is a free selection from Wikipedia designed for education towards children eight to seventeen.[[W 104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-369)

There have been efforts to put a select subset of Wikipedia's articles into printed book form.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WP_into_books_1-370)[[W 105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WP_schools_selection_1-371) Since 2009, tens of thousands of [print-on-demand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Print_on_demand "Print on demand") books that reproduced English, German, Russian, and French Wikipedia articles have been produced by the American company [Books LLC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Books_LLC "Books LLC") and by three Mauritian subsidiaries of the German publisher [VDM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VDM_Publishing "VDM Publishing").[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-FAZ-372)

The website [DBpedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DBpedia "DBpedia"), begun in 2007, extracts data from the infoboxes and category declarations of the English-language Wikipedia.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-373) Wikimedia has created the [Wikidata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikidata "Wikidata") project with a similar objective of storing the basic facts from each page of Wikipedia and other Wikimedia Foundation projects and make it available in a queryable [semantic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_Web "Semantic Web") format, [RDF](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource_Description_Framework "Resource Description Framework").[[W 106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-374) As of February 2023, it has over 101 million items.[[W 107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-375)[WikiReader](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WikiReader "WikiReader") is a dedicated reader device that contains an offline copy of Wikipedia, which was launched by [OpenMoko](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Openmoko "Openmoko") and first released in 2009.[[W 108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-376)

Obtaining the full contents of Wikipedia for reuse presents challenges, since direct cloning via a [web crawler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_crawler "Web crawler") is discouraged.[[W 109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WP_DB_usage_policy_1-377) Wikipedia publishes "[dumps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Database_download "Wikipedia:Database download")" of its contents, but these are text-only; as of 2023, there is no dump available of Wikipedia's images.[[W 110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WP_image_data_dumps_1-378)[Wikimedia Enterprise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikimedia_Enterprise "Wikimedia Enterprise") is a for-profit solution to this.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-379)

Several languages of Wikipedia also maintain a reference desk, where volunteers answer questions from the general public. According to a study by Pnina Shachaf in the _[Journal of Documentation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Journal\_of\_Documentation "Journal of Documentation")_, the quality of the Wikipedia reference desk is comparable to a standard library [reference desk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reference_desk "Reference desk"), with an accuracy of 55 percent.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-380)

#### Mobile access

[![Image 21](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Wikipedia_on_Mobile_screenshot_%282024%29_%28cropped%29.png/250px-Wikipedia_on_Mobile_screenshot_%282024%29_%28cropped%29.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wikipedia_on_Mobile_screenshot_(2024)_(cropped).png)

A mobile version showing the English Wikipedia's Main Page on October 2, 2024

Wikipedia's original medium was for users to read and edit content using any standard [web browser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_browser "Web browser") through a fixed [Internet connection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_access "Internet access"). Although Wikipedia content has been accessible through the [mobile web](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mobile_web "Mobile web") since July 2013, _The New York Times_ on February 9, 2014, quoted [Erik Möller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erik_M%C3%B6ller "Erik Möller"), deputy director of the Wikimedia Foundation, stating that the transition of internet traffic from desktops to mobile devices was significant and a cause for concern and worry. The article in _The New York Times_ reported the comparison statistics for mobile edits stating that, "Only 20 percent of the readership of the English-language Wikipedia comes via mobile devices, a figure substantially lower than the percentage of mobile traffic for other media sites, many of which approach 50 percent. And the shift to mobile editing has lagged even more." In 2014 _The New York Times_ reported that Möller has assigned "a team of 10 software developers focused on mobile", out of a total of approximately 200 employees working at the Wikimedia Foundation. One principal concern cited by _The New York Times_ for the "worry" is for Wikipedia to effectively address attrition issues with the number of editors which the online encyclopedia attracts to edit and maintain its content in a mobile access environment.[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-small_screen-67) By 2023, the Wikimedia Foundation's staff had grown to over 700 employees.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WF10.23.23-5)

Access to Wikipedia from mobile phones was possible as early as 2004, through the [Wireless Application Protocol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wireless_Application_Protocol "Wireless Application Protocol") (WAP), via the [Wapedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wapedia "Wapedia") service.[[W 99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:16-363) In June 2007, Wikipedia launched en.mobile.wikipedia.org, an official website for wireless devices. In 2009, a newer mobile service was officially released, located at en.m.wikipedia.org, which caters to more advanced mobile devices such as the [iPhone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone "IPhone"), [Android](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Android_(operating_system) "Android (operating system)")-based devices, or [WebOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WebOS "WebOS")-based devices.[[W 111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WM_mobile_added_1-381) Several other methods of mobile access to Wikipedia have emerged since. Many devices and applications optimize or enhance the display of Wikipedia content for mobile devices, while some also incorporate additional features such as use of Wikipedia [metadata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metadata "Metadata") like [geoinformation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geographic_data_and_information "Geographic data and information").[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-androgeoid.com_LPOI_WP_1-382)[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-ilounge_iphone_gems_WP-383)

The Android app for Wikipedia was released in January 2012, to over 500,000 installs and generally positive reviews, scoring over four of a possible five in a poll of approximately 200,000 users downloading from Google.[[W 112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-384)[[W 113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-385) The version for iOS was released on April 3, 2013, to similar reviews.[[W 114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-386)[Wikipedia Zero](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia_Zero "Wikipedia Zero") was an initiative of the Wikimedia Foundation to expand the reach of the encyclopedia to the developing countries by partnering with mobile operators to allow free access.[[W 115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:17-387)[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-388) It was discontinued in February 2018 due to lack of participation from mobile operators.[[W 115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:17-387)

[Andrew Lih](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Lih "Andrew Lih") and [Andrew Brown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Brown_(writer) "Andrew Brown (writer)") both maintain editing Wikipedia with [smartphones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smartphone "Smartphone") is difficult and this discourages new potential contributors.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:18-389)[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:19-390) Lih states that the number of Wikipedia editors has been declining after several years,[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:18-389) and Tom Simonite of _[MIT Technology Review](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIT\_Technology\_Review "MIT Technology Review")_ claims the bureaucratic structure and rules are a factor in this. Simonite alleges some [Wikipedians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedian "Wikipedian") use the labyrinthine rules and guidelines to dominate others and those editors have a vested interest in keeping the status quo.[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Simonite-2013-50) Lih alleges there is a serious disagreement among existing contributors on how to resolve this. Lih fears for Wikipedia's long-term future while Brown fears problems with Wikipedia will remain and rival encyclopedias will not replace it.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:18-389)[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:19-390)

### Chinese access

Access to Wikipedia has been [blocked](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_China "Internet censorship in China") in [mainland China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainland_China "Mainland China") since May 2015.[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:1-11)[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-391)[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-392) This was done after Wikipedia started to use [HTTPS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTTPS "HTTPS") encryption, which made selective censorship more difficult.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-393)

Cultural influence
------------------

### Trusted source to combat fake news

In 2017–18, after a barrage of false news reports, both Facebook and YouTube announced they would rely on Wikipedia to help their users evaluate reports and reject false news.[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:20-394)[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-auto-395)[Noam Cohen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noam_Cohen "Noam Cohen"), writing in _[The Washington Post](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Washington\_Post "The Washington Post")_ states, "YouTube's reliance on Wikipedia to set the record straight builds on the thinking of another fact-challenged platform, the Facebook social network, which announced last year that Wikipedia would help its users root out '[fake news](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fake_news "Fake news")'."[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-auto-395)[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-396)

### Readership

In February 2014, _The New York Times_ reported that Wikipedia was ranked fifth globally among all websites, stating "With 18 billion page views and nearly 500 million unique visitors a month,... Wikipedia trails just Yahoo, Facebook, Microsoft and Google, the largest with 1.2 billion unique visitors."[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-small_screen-67) However, its ranking dropped to 13th globally by June 2020 due mostly to a rise in popularity of Chinese websites for online shopping.[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Alexa-81) The website has since recovered its ranking as of April 2022.[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Alexa-81)

In addition to [logistic growth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logistic_function "Logistic function") in the number of its articles,[[W 116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-modelling-397) Wikipedia has steadily gained status as a general reference website since its inception in 2001.[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-comscore-398) The number of readers of Wikipedia worldwide reached 365 million at the end of 2009.[[W 117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-365M-399) The [Pew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pew_Research_Center "Pew Research Center") Internet and American Life project found that one third of US Internet users consulted Wikipedia.[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Wikipedia_users-400) In 2011, _[Business Insider](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Business\_Insider "Business Insider")_ gave Wikipedia a valuation of $4 billion if it ran advertisements.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-401)

According to "Wikipedia Readership Survey 2011", the average age of Wikipedia readers is 36, with a rough parity between genders. Almost half of Wikipedia readers visit the site more than five times a month, and a similar number of readers specifically look for Wikipedia in search engine results. About 47 percent of Wikipedia readers do not realize that Wikipedia is a non-profit organization.[[W 118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-402) As of February 2023, Wikipedia attracts around 2 billion unique devices monthly, with the English Wikipedia receiving 10 billion [pageviews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Pageview_statistics "Wikipedia:Pageview statistics") each month.[[W 1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Wikimedia_Stats-8)

#### COVID-19 pandemic

During the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic "COVID-19 pandemic"), Wikipedia's coverage of the pandemic and fight against misinformation received international media attention, and brought an increase in Wikipedia readership overall.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-403)[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:21-404)[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-405)[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-406) Noam Cohen wrote in _[Wired](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wired\_(magazine) "Wired (magazine)")_ that Wikipedia's effort to combat [misinformation related to the pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_misinformation "COVID-19 misinformation") was different from other major websites, opining, "Unless Twitter, Facebook and [the others](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_media "Social media") can learn to address misinformation more effectively, Wikipedia will remain the last best place on the Internet."[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-:21-404) In October 2020, the [World Health Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization "World Health Organization") announced they were freely licensing its [infographics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infographic "Infographic") and other materials on Wikimedia projects.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-407) There were nearly 7,000 COVID-19 related Wikipedia articles across 188 different Wikipedias, as of November 2021.[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-408)[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-409)

### Cultural significance

[![Image 22](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Wikipedia_Monument_2.JPG/250px-Wikipedia_Monument_2.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wikipedia_Monument_2.JPG)

_[Wikipedia Monument](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia\_Monument "Wikipedia Monument")_ in [Słubice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S%C5%82ubice "Słubice"), Poland, by [Mihran Hakobyan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mihran_Hakobyan "Mihran Hakobyan") (2014)

Wikipedia's content has also been used in academic studies, books, conferences, and court cases.[[W 119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Wikipedia_in_media-410)[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Bourgeois-411)[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-ssrn.com_Wikipedian_Justice_1-412) The [Parliament of Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliament_of_Canada "Parliament of Canada")'s website refers to Wikipedia's article on [same-sex marriage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Same-sex_marriage "Same-sex marriage") in the "related links" section of its "further reading" list for the _[Civil Marriage Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil\_Marriage\_Act "Civil Marriage Act")_.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-parl.gc.ca_same-sex_marriage-413) The encyclopedia's assertions are increasingly used as a source by organizations such as the US federal courts and the [World Intellectual Property Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Organization "World Intellectual Property Organization")[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WP_court_source-414)—though mainly for supporting information rather than information decisive to a case.[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Courts_turn_to_Wikipedia-415) Content appearing on Wikipedia has also been cited as a source and referenced in some [US intelligence agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Intelligence_Community "United States Intelligence Community") reports.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-US_Intelligence-416) In December 2008, the scientific journal _[RNA Biology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RNA\_Biology "RNA Biology")_ launched a new section for descriptions of families of RNA molecules and requires authors who contribute to the section to also submit a draft article on the [RNA family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rfam "Rfam") for publication in Wikipedia.[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Declan-417) Wikipedia has also been used as a source in journalism,[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-ajr.org_WP_in_the_newsroom-418)[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-twsY23-419) often without attribution, and several reporters have been dismissed for [plagiarizing from Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plagiarism_from_Wikipedia "Plagiarism from Wikipedia").[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-shizuoka_plagiarized_WP_1-420)[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-421)[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-starbulletin.com_Inquiry_prompts_dismissal-422)[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-423)

In 2006, _[Time](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time\_(magazine) "Time (magazine)")_ magazine recognized Wikipedia's participation (along with YouTube, [Reddit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reddit "Reddit"), [MySpace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MySpace "MySpace"), and Facebook) in the rapid growth of online collaboration and interaction by millions of people worldwide.[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-Time2006-424) On September 16, 2007, _[The Washington Post](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Washington\_Post "The Washington Post")_ reported that Wikipedia had become a focal point in the [2008 US election campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_United_States_presidential_election "2008 United States presidential election"), saying: "Type a candidate's name into Google, and among the first results is a Wikipedia page, making those entries arguably as important as any ad in defining a candidate. Already, the presidential entries are being edited, dissected and debated countless times each day."[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-WP.com_WP_election_usage-425) An October 2007 [Reuters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reuters "Reuters") article, titled "Wikipedia page the latest status symbol", reported the recent phenomenon of how having a Wikipedia article vindicates one's notability.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-426)

One of the first times Wikipedia was involved in a governmental affair was on September 28, 2007, when [Italian politician](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_of_Italy "Politics of Italy")[Franco Grillini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franco_Grillini "Franco Grillini") raised a parliamentary question with the minister of cultural resources and activities about the necessity of [freedom of panorama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_panorama "Freedom of panorama"). He said that the lack of such freedom forced Wikipedia, "the seventh most consulted website", to forbid all images of modern Italian buildings and art, and claimed this was hugely damaging to tourist revenues.[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-427)

Wikipedia, an introduction – [Erasmus Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erasmus_Prize "Erasmus Prize") 2015

[![Image 23](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Quadriga-verleihung-rr-02.jpg/250px-Quadriga-verleihung-rr-02.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Quadriga-verleihung-rr-02.jpg)

[Jimmy Wales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Wales "Jimmy Wales") accepts the 2008 [Quadriga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadriga_(award) "Quadriga (award)")_A Mission of Enlightenment_ award on behalf of Wikipedia.

A working group led by [Peter Stone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Stone_(professor) "Peter Stone (professor)") (formed as a part of the [Stanford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford "Stanford")-based project [One Hundred Year Study on Artificial Intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One_Hundred_Year_Study_on_Artificial_Intelligence "One Hundred Year Study on Artificial Intelligence")) in its report called Wikipedia "the best-known example of crowdsourcing... that far exceeds traditionally-compiled information sources, such as encyclopedias and dictionaries, in scale and depth".[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-428)[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-NYT-20230718-429)

In a 2017 opinion piece for _[Wired](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wired\_(magazine) "Wired (magazine)")_, [Hossein Derakhshan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hossein_Derakhshan "Hossein Derakhshan") describes Wikipedia as "one of the last remaining pillars of the [open](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Openness "Openness") and [decentralized web](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decentralization#Centralization_and_redecentralization_of_the_Internet "Decentralization")" and contrasted its existence as a text-based source of knowledge with social media and [social networking services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_networking_service "Social networking service"), the latter having "since colonized the web for television's values". For Derakhshan, Wikipedia's goal as an encyclopedia represents the [Age of Enlightenment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment "Age of Enlightenment") tradition of [rationality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rationality "Rationality") triumphing over emotions, a trend which he considers "endangered" due to the "gradual shift from a [typographic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typography "Typography") culture to a photographic one, which in turn mean[s] a shift from rationality to emotions, exposition to entertainment". Rather than "_[sapere aude](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sapere\_aude "Sapere aude")_" ([lit.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literal_translation "Literal translation")'dare to know'), social networks have led to a culture of "dare not to care to know". This is while Wikipedia faces "a more concerning problem" than funding, namely "a flattening growth rate in the number of contributors to the website". Consequently, the challenge for Wikipedia and those who use it is to "save Wikipedia and its promise of a free and open collection of all human knowledge amid the conquest of new and old television—how to collect and preserve knowledge when nobody cares to know."[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-430)

#### Awards

[![Image 24](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Wikipedia_team_visiting_to_Parliament_of_Oviedo_Spain_2015.JPG/250px-Wikipedia_team_visiting_to_Parliament_of_Oviedo_Spain_2015.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wikipedia_team_visiting_to_Parliament_of_Oviedo_Spain_2015.JPG)

Wikipedia team visiting the Parliament of Asturias

[![Image 25](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Spanish_Wikipedians_meetup.jpg/250px-Spanish_Wikipedians_meetup.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Spanish_Wikipedians_meetup.jpg)

Wikipedians meeting after the 2015 Asturias awards ceremony

Wikipedia has won many awards, receiving its first two major awards in May 2004.[[W 120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-431) The first was a Golden Nica for Digital Communities of the annual [Prix Ars Electronica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prix_Ars_Electronica "Prix Ars Electronica") contest; this came with a €10,000 (£6,588; $12,700) grant and an invitation to present at the PAE Cyberarts Festival in Austria later that year. The second was a Judges' [Webby Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Webby_Award "Webby Award") for the "community" category.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia#cite_note-webbyawards_WP_awards_1-432)
